24:I[78891,["529","static/chunks/529-b3a318fab494e03f.js","244","static/chunks/244-f8e89f92ed6eb924.js","839","static/chunks/839-b514104c7e948606.js","165","static/chunks/165-ae3b45f0d86ef78d.js","184","static/chunks/app/dashboard/roots/%5Broot%5D/page-e0a9e2c37c8cb20d.js"],"CardTitle"]
25:T4dc,You who believe, when you contract a debt for a stated term, put it down in writing: have a scribe write it down justly between you. No scribe should refuse to write: let him write as God has taught him, let the debtor dictate, and let him fear God, his Lord, and not diminish &#91;the debt&#93; at all. If the debtor is feeble-minded, weak, or unable to dictate, then let his guardian dictate justly. Call in two men as witnesses. If two men are not there, then call one man and two women out of those you approve as witnesses, so that if one of the two women should forget the other can remind her. Let the witnesses not refuse when they are summoned. Do not disdain to write the debt down, be it small or large, along with the time it falls due: this way is more equitable in God&rsquo;s eyes, more reliable as testimony, and more likely to prevent doubts arising between you. But if the merchandise is there and you hand it over, there is no blame on you if you do not write it down. Have witnesses present whenever you trade with one another, and let no harm be done to either scribe or witness, for if you did cause them harm, it would be a crime on your part. Be mindful of God, and He will teach you: He has full knowledge of everything26:T4dc,You who believe, when you contract a debt for a stated term, put it down in writing: have a scribe write it down justly between you.                   </form>, (S, A, Mgh, L, Msb, K,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">شَهَدَ</orth>
                  </form>; (K;) and <foreign lang="ar">شَهُدَ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">شَهُدَ</orth>
                  </form>; (K;) also pronounced and written <foreign lang="ar">شَهْدَ</foreign>, (Akh, S, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">شِهْدَ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">شِهِدَ</foreign>, accord. to a rule applying to all verbs of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعِلَ</foreign> of which the medial radical letter is a faucial; (MF;) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">شَهَادَةٌ</foreign> (S, A, Mgh, L, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">شهد</foreign>; (TA;) [there written without any syll. sign, and not found by me in any other Lex.;]) <hi rend="ital">He told,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">gave information of, what he had witnessed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">seen</hi> or <hi rend="ital">beheld with his eye:</hi> (Mgh, L, Msb:) this is the primary signification: (L:) <hi rend="ital">he declared what he knew: he gave testimony, attestation,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evidence; he bore witness:</hi> (L:) <hi rend="ital">he gave decisive information.</hi> (S, A, L, K.) [See also <foreign lang="ar">شَهَادَةٌ</foreign> below.] You say, <foreign lang="ar">شَهِدَ بِكَذَا</foreign>, inf. n. as above, (S, A, Mgh, L, Msb, K,) <hi rend="ital">He told,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">gave information of, such a thing, as having witnessed it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">seen</hi> or <hi rend="ital">beheld it with his eye;</hi> (Mgh, Msb;) or <hi rend="ital">declared such a thing as knowing it;</hi> (L;) or <hi rend="ital">gave his testimony, attestation,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evidence, respecting it;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">bore witness of it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to it;</hi> (S, A, L, K;) <foreign lang="ar">عِنْدَ الحَاكِمِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">in the presence of the judge</hi>]; <foreign lang="ar">لِفُلَانٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">for,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in favour of, such a one</hi>], (S, Mgh, L, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى فُلَانٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">against,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in opposition to, such a one</hi>]. (Mgh.) And <foreign lang="ar">شَهِدَ عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He gave decisive information</hi> [<hi rend="ital">respecting such a thing</hi> (as in the Kur xlvi. 9, and in many other instances); <hi rend="ital">he testified respecting it</hi>]. (S, L. [See also another meaning of this phrase in what follows.]) [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">شَهِدَ ٱللّٰهُ أَنَّهُ لَا إِلَاهَ إِلَّا هُوَ</foreign>, in the Kur [iii. 16], means <hi rend="ital">God hath given evidence that there is no deity but He:</hi> (Abu-l- 'Abbás, IAmb, Jel:) or <hi rend="ital">God knoweth</hi> &amp;c.; (Ah- mad Ibn-Yahyà, K;) and so <foreign lang="ar">شَهِدَ ٱللّٰهُ</foreign> throughout the Kur-án: (Ahmad Ibn-Yahyà:) or <hi rend="ital">God saith</hi> &amp;c.: or <hi rend="ital">God hath written</hi> &amp;c.                   <hi rend="ital">An angel:</hi> (S, L, K:) or <hi rend="ital">a guardian angel:</hi> (Mujáhid:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">أَشْهَادٌ</foreign>: or this means the <hi rend="ital">prophets.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And The <hi rend="ital">tongue:</hi> (S, L, K:) from the saying, <foreign lang="ar">لِفُلَانٍ شَاهِدٌ حَسَنٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Such a one has an elegant diction.</hi> (L.) One says also, <foreign lang="ar">مَا لِفُلَانٍ رُوَآءٌ وَلَا شَاهِدٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Such a one has neither goodliness of aspect nor tongue.</hi> (Aboo-Bekr, L.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  [As a conventional term used in lexicology &amp;c.,] <hi rend="ital">An evidential example,</hi> generally poetical, of the form or meaning of a word or phrase: pl. <foreign lang="ar">شَوَاهِدُ</foreign>: the sciences that require <foreign lang="ar">شَوَاهِد</foreign> being those of <foreign lang="ar">اللُّغَة</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">الصَّرْف</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">النَّحْو</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">المَعَانِى</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">البَيَان</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">البَدِيع</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">العَرُوض</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">القَوَافِى</foreign>. (MF on the <foreign lang="ar">خُطْبَة</foreign> of the K.) [One says, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا شَاهِدٌ لِكَذَا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى كَذَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">This is an evidential example of such a thing.</hi>] With respect to the classical language, absolutely, <foreign lang="ar">شواهد</foreign> are taken, by universal consent, from the Kur-án, and from the language [both verse and prose (Kull p. 348)] of those Arabs who lived before the period of the corruption [in any considerable degree] of the Arabic tongue: [see <foreign lang="ar">مُوَلَّدٌ</foreign>:] also, accord. to the general decision of the learned, from the Traditions of Mohammad; [which last source is excluded by some because traditions may be corrupted in language by their transmitters, and interpolated, and even forged;] and electively from the language of those Arabs who lived after the first corruption of the Arabic tongue, but before the corruption had become extensive. (Mz, 1st <foreign lang="ar">نوع</foreign>; and MF ubi suprà. [See, again, <foreign lang="ar">مُوَلَّدٌ</foreign>.]) The classes of the poets from whose poetry <foreign lang="ar">شواهد</foreign> are taken are the Pagan Arabs, the Mukhadrams, the Islámees, and the Muwelleds: [see <foreign lang="ar">جَاهِلِىٌّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مُخَضْرَمٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">إِسْلَامِىٌّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مُوَلَّدٌ</foreign>:] with respect to all the sciences above mentioned, they are taken from the poetry of the first, second, and third, classes; from that of the first and second by universal consent, and from that of the third electively: (MF ubi suprá:) but they are taken from the poetry of the fourth class with respect only to the sciences of <foreign lang="ar">المَعَانِى</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">البَيَان</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">البَدِيع</foreign>. (Idem, and Kull p. 348.) [The age of the earliest existing classical poems (though some older fragments and couplets and single verses have been preserved) is only about a century before the birth of Mohammad: that of the latest, about a century after his death. (See the Preface to this work.)]          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">Knowing,</hi> (Msb,) <hi rend="ital">and witnessing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">seeing</hi> or <hi rend="ital">beholding with his eye; a witness,</hi> as meaning <hi rend="ital">an eyewitness;</hi> (L, Msb;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n23197-6" target="شَهِيدٌ" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n23193"/></foreign>: pl. of the former [or, as is said in the L in art. <foreign lang="ar">مجد</foreign>, of the former or of the latter,] <foreign lang="ar">أَشْهَادٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">شُهُودٌ</foreign>; [but see what is said of these pls. in the first sentence of this paragraph;] and of the latter <foreign lang="ar">شُهَدَآءُ</foreign>. (Msb.) [See an ex. of   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n23197-7" target="شَهِيدٌ" n="7" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n23193"/></foreign> in this sense in a verse cited voce <foreign lang="ar">رَبٌّ</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  [Hence, in the present day, applied to <hi rend="ital">A notary, who hears and writes and attests cases to be submitted for judgment in the court of a kádee.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">Present; a witness</hi> as meaning <hi rend="ital">one personally present;</hi> (S, L, Msb, K;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n23197-8" target="شَهِيدٌ" n="8" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n23193"/></foreign>: (Msb:) pl. of the former <foreign lang="ar">شُهَّدٌ</foreign> (S, L, K) [and <foreign lang="ar">أَشْهَادٌ</foreign>, as above,] and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n23197-9" target="شُهُودٌ" n="9" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n23192"/></foreign>, (K,) or this last is used as a pl. but is originally an inf. n. (S, L.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">الشَّاهِدُ يَرَى مَا لَا يَرَى الغَائِبُ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">The present knows what the absent knows not.</hi> (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">قَوْمٌ شُهُودٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">People,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">persons, present.</hi> (S, A.) And <foreign lang="ar">كَلَّمْتُهُ عَلَى رُؤُوسِ الأَشْهَادِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I spoke to him before witnesses,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">persons present</hi>]. (A.)          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  [Hence, app., being opposed to <foreign lang="ar">غَائِبٌ</foreign>,] <hi rend="ital">A running in which a horse exerts his force unsparingly;</hi> (A, L;) as in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">لِلْفَرَسِ غَائِبٌ وَشَاهِدٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The horse has a run which he reserves</hi> [<hi rend="ital">for the time of need</hi>], <hi rend="ital">and a run which he performs unsparingly;</hi> like the saying, <foreign lang="ar">لَهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">صَوْنٌ وَبَذْلٌ</foreign>: (A: [see 1 in art. <foreign lang="ar">بذل</foreign>:]) or <foreign lang="ar">شَاهِدٌ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">a running that testifies the excellence of a horse,</hi> (IAar, K,) <hi rend="ital">and his quality of outstripping others.</hi> (IAar, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="10">-b10-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">A star</hi> [app. <hi rend="ital">when visible</hi>]; (Aboo-Eiyoob, K;) as being present and apparent in the night. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="11">-b11-</sense>  [Hence, accord. to some,] <foreign lang="ar">صَلَاةُ الشَّاهِدِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The prayer of sunset;</hi> (A, L, Msb, K;) because it is <hi rend="ital">the prayer that is performed when the star becomes visible;</hi> (Sh, L;) also called <foreign lang="ar">صَلَاةُ البَصَرِ</foreign>, because the stars are seen at the time thereof: or, accord. to some, <hi rend="ital">the prayer of daybreak;</hi> (L;) [and so, accord. to some, <foreign lang="ar">صَلَاةُ البَصَرِ</foreign>; (see art. <foreign lang="ar">بصر</foreign>;)] as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n23197-10" target="المَشْهُودُ" n="10" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (TA;) and it is said to be so called because he who is travelling must perform it without abridging it, like him who is present at his home: Aboo-Sa'eed Ed-Dareer says that the former prayer is so called for this reason [as is also said in the A and Msb]: AM asserts that the first reason assigned above is the right one, because the prayer of daybreak, in like manner, may not be abridged, and is not thus called; but it is thus called by a poet. (L.)          <sense type="b" n="12">-b12-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">الشَّاهِدُ</foreign> is a name of <hi rend="ital">Friday;</hi> (Fr, K;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n23197-11" target="المَشْهُودُ" n="11" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>: or the latter is <hi rend="ital">the day of resurrection:</hi> (K:) or <hi rend="ital">the day of 'Arafeh:</hi> (Fr, K: [see <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفَةُ</foreign>:]) because of the presence and congregation of people on each of those days. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="13">-b13-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">شَاهِدٌ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">Matter resembling mucus, that comes forth with the fœtus:</hi> (S, K:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">شُهُودٌ</foreign>: which latter, accord. to ISd, means the <foreign lang="ar">أَغْرَاس</foreign> [pl. of <foreign lang="ar">غِرْسٌ</foreign>, q. v.,] <hi rend="ital">upon the head of a young camel at the time of its birth.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">شُهُودٌ النَّاقَةِ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">The marks left by the blood,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by the membrane that enclosed the fœtus, of the she-camel, in the place where she has brought forth.</hi> (S, K.)          <sense type="b" n="14">-b14-</sense>  Also A <hi rend="ital">quick,</hi> or an <hi rend="ital">expeditious,</hi> thing or affair.
